{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01N9jH7z8dYAFG7uWGm8NpHS","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Task Master\n     2→\n     3→### by [@eyaltoledano](https://x.com/eyaltoledano)\n     4→\n     5→A task management system for AI-driven development with Claude, designed to work seamlessly with Cursor AI.\n     6→\n     7→## Requirements\n     8→\n     9→- Node.js 14.0.0 or higher\n    10→- Anthropic API key (Claude API)\n    11→- Anthropic SDK version 0.39.0 or higher\n    12→- OpenAI SDK (for Perplexity API integration, optional)\n    13→\n    14→## Configuration\n    15→\n    16→Taskmaster uses two primary configuration methods:\n    17→\n    18→1.  **`.taskmasterconfig` File (Project Root)**\n    19→\n    20→    - Stores most settings: AI model selections (main, research, fallback), parameters (max tokens, temperature), logging level, default priority/subtasks, project name.\n    21→    - **Created and managed using `task-master models --setup` CLI command or the `models` MCP tool.**\n    22→    - Do not edit manually unless you know what you are doing.\n    23→\n    24→2.  **Environment Variables (`.env` file or MCP `env` block)**\n    25→    - Used **only** for sensitive **API Keys** (e.g., `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY`, etc.) and specific endpoints (like `OLLAMA_BASE_URL`).\n    26→    - **For CLI:** Place keys in a `.env` file in your project root.\n    27→    - **For MCP/Cursor:** Place keys in the `env` section of your `.cursor/mcp.json` (or other MCP config according to the AI IDE or client you use) file under the `taskmaster-ai` server definition.\n    28→\n    29→**Important:** Settings like model choices, max tokens, temperature, and log level are **no longer configured via environment variables.** Use the `task-master models` command or tool.\n    30→\n    31→See the [Configuration Guide](docs/configuration.md) for full details.\n    32→\n    33→## Installation\n    34→\n    35→```bash\n    36→# Install globally\n    37→npm install -g task-master-ai\n    38→\n    39→# OR install locally within your project\n    40→npm install task-master-ai\n    41→```\n    42→\n    43→### Initialize a new project\n    44→\n    45→```bash\n    46→# If installed globally\n    47→task-master init\n    48→\n    49→# If installed locally\n    50→npx task-master init\n    51→```\n    52→\n    53→This will prompt you for project details and set up a new project with the necessary files and structure.\n    54→\n    55→### Important Notes\n    56→\n    57→1. **ES Modules Configuration:**\n    58→\n    59→   - This project uses ES Modules (ESM) instead of CommonJS.\n    60→   - This is set via `\"type\": \"module\"` in your package.json.\n    61→   - Use `import/export` syntax instead of `require()`.\n    62→   - Files should use `.js` or `.mjs` extensions.\n    63→   - To use a CommonJS module, either:\n    64→     - Rename it with `.cjs` extension\n    65→     - Use `await import()` for dynamic imports\n    66→   - If you need CommonJS throughout your project, remove `\"type\": \"module\"` from package.json, but Task Master scripts expect ESM.\n    67→\n    68→2. The Anthropic SDK version should be 0.39.0 or higher.\n    69→\n    70→## Quick Start with Global Commands\n    71→\n    72→After installing the package globally, you can use these CLI commands from any directory:\n    73→\n    74→```bash\n    75→# Initialize a new project\n    76→task-master init\n    77→\n    78→# Parse a PRD and generate tasks\n    79→task-master parse-prd your-prd.txt\n    80→\n    81→# List all tasks\n    82→task-master list\n    83→\n    84→# Show the next task to work on\n    85→task-master next\n    86→\n    87→# Generate task files\n    88→task-master generate\n    89→```\n    90→\n    91→## Troubleshooting\n    92→\n    93→### If `task-master init` doesn't respond:\n    94→\n    95→Try running it with Node directly:\n    96→\n    97→```bash\n    98→node node_modules/claude-task-master/scripts/init.js\n    99→```\n   100→\n   101→Or clone the repository and run:\n   102→\n   103→```bash\n   104→git clone https://github.com/eyaltoledano/claude-task-master.git\n   105→cd claude-task-master\n   106→node scripts/init.js\n   107→```\n   108→\n   109→## Task Structure\n   110→\n   111→Tasks in tasks.json have the following structure:\n   112→\n   113→- `id`: Unique identifier for the task (Example: `1`)\n   114→- `title`: Brief, descriptive title of the task (Example: `\"Initialize Repo\"`)\n   115→- `description`: Concise description of what the task involves (Example: `\"Create a new repository, set up initial structure.\"`)\n   116→- `status`: Current state of the task (Example: `\"pending\"`, `\"done\"`, `\"deferred\"`)\n   117→- `dependencies`: IDs of tasks that must be completed before this task (Example: `[1, 2]`)\n   118→  - Dependencies are displayed with status indicators (✅ for completed, ⏱️ for pending)\n   119→  - This helps quickly identify which prerequisite tasks are blocking work\n   120→- `priority`: Importance level of the task (Example: `\"high\"`, `\"medium\"`, `\"low\"`)\n   121→- `details`: In-depth implementation instructions (Example: `\"Use GitHub client ID/secret, handle callback, set session token.\"`)\n   122→- `testStrategy`: Verification approach (Example: `\"Deploy and call endpoint to confirm 'Hello World' response.\"`)\n   123→- `subtasks`: List of smaller, more specific tasks that make up the main task (Example: `[{\"id\": 1, \"title\": \"Configure OAuth\", ...}]`)\n   124→\n   125→## Integrating with Cursor AI\n   126→\n   127→Claude Task Master is designed to work seamlessly with [Cursor AI](https://www.cursor.so/), providing a structured workflow for AI-driven development.\n   128→\n   129→### Setup with Cursor\n   130→\n   131→1. After initializing your project, open it in Cursor\n   132→2. The `.cursor/rules/dev_workflow.mdc` file is automatically loaded by Cursor, providing the AI with knowledge about the task management system\n   133→3. Place your PRD document in the `scripts/` directory (e.g., `scripts/prd.txt`)\n   134→4. Open Cursor's AI chat and switch to Agent mode\n   135→\n   136→### Setting up MCP in Cursor\n   137→\n   138→To enable enhanced task management capabilities directly within Cursor using the Model Control Protocol (MCP):\n   139→\n   140→1. Go to Cursor settings\n   141→2. Navigate to the MCP section\n   142→3. Click on \"Add New MCP Server\"\n   143→4. Configure with the following details:\n   144→   - Name: \"Task Master\"\n   145→   - Type: \"Command\"\n   146→   - Command: \"npx -y task-master-ai\"\n   147→5. Save the settings\n   148→\n   149→Once configured, you can interact with Task Master's task management commands directly through Cursor's interface, providing a more integrated experience.\n   150→\n   151→### Initial Task Generation\n   152→\n   153→In Cursor's AI chat, instruct the agent to generate tasks from your PRD:\n   154→\n   155→```\n   156→Please use the task-master parse-prd command to generate tasks from my PRD. The PRD is located at scripts/prd.txt.\n   157→```\n   158→\n   159→The agent will execute:\n   160→\n   161→```bash\n   162→task-master parse-prd scripts/prd.txt\n   163→```\n   164→\n   165→This will:\n   166→\n   167→- Parse your PRD document\n   168→- Generate a structured `tasks.json` file with tasks, dependencies, priorities, and test strategies\n   169→- The agent will understand this process due to the Cursor rules\n   170→\n   171→### Generate Individual Task Files\n   172→\n   173→Next, ask the agent to generate individual task files:\n   174→\n   175→```\n   176→Please generate individual task files from tasks.json\n   177→```\n   178→\n   179→The agent will execute:\n   180→\n   181→```bash\n   182→task-master generate\n   183→```\n   184→\n   185→This creates individual task files in the `tasks/` directory (e.g., `task_001.txt`, `task_002.txt`), making it easier to reference specific tasks.\n   186→\n   187→## AI-Driven Development Workflow\n   188→\n   189→The Cursor agent is pre-configured (via the rules file) to follow this workflow:\n   190→\n   191→### 1. Task Discovery and Selection\n   192→\n   193→Ask the agent to list available tasks:\n   194→\n   195→```\n   196→What tasks are available to work on next?\n   197→```\n   198→\n   199→The agent will:\n   200→\n   201→- Run `task-master list` to see all tasks\n   202→- Run `task-master next` to determine the next task to work on\n   203→- Analyze dependencies to determine which tasks are ready to be worked on\n   204→- Prioritize tasks based on priority level and ID order\n   205→- Suggest the next task(s) to implement\n   206→\n   207→### 2. Task Implementation\n   208→\n   209→When implementing a task, the agent will:\n   210→\n   211→- Reference the task's details section for implementation specifics\n   212→- Consider dependencies on previous tasks\n   213→- Follow the project's coding standards\n   214→- Create appropriate tests based on the task's testStrategy\n   215→\n   216→You can ask:\n   217→\n   218→```\n   219→Let's implement task 3. What does it involve?\n   220→```\n   221→\n   222→### 3. Task Verification\n   223→\n   224→Before marking a task as complete, verify it according to:\n   225→\n   226→- The task's specified testStrategy\n   227→- Any automated tests in the codebase\n   228→- Manual verification if required\n   229→\n   230→### 4. Task Completion\n   231→\n   232→When a task is completed, tell the agent:\n   233→\n   234→```\n   235→Task 3 is now complete. Please update its status.\n   236→```\n   237→\n   238→The agent will execute:\n   239→\n   240→```bash\n   241→task-master set-status --id=3 --status=done\n   242→```\n   243→\n   244→### 5. Handling Implementation Drift\n   245→\n   246→If during implementation, you discover that:\n   247→\n   248→- The current approach differs significantly from what was planned\n   249→- Future tasks need to be modified due to current implementation choices\n   250→- New dependencies or requirements have emerged\n   251→\n   252→Tell the agent:\n   253→\n   254→```\n   255→We've changed our approach. We're now using Express instead of Fastify. Please update all future tasks to reflect this change.\n   256→```\n   257→\n   258→The agent will execute:\n   259→\n   260→```bash\n   261→task-master update --from=4 --prompt=\"Now we are using Express instead of Fastify.\"\n   262→```\n   263→\n   264→This will rewrite or re-scope subsequent tasks in tasks.json while preserving completed work.\n   265→\n   266→### 6. Breaking Down Complex Tasks\n   267→\n   268→For complex tasks that need more granularity:\n   269→\n   270→```\n   271→Task 5 seems complex. Can you break it down into subtasks?\n   272→```\n   273→\n   274→The agent will execute:\n   275→\n   276→```bash\n   277→task-master expand --id=5 --num=3\n   278→```\n   279→\n   280→You can provide additional context:\n   281→\n   282→```\n   283→Please break down task 5 with a focus on security considerations.\n   284→```\n   285→\n   286→The agent will execute:\n   287→\n   288→```bash\n   289→task-master expand --id=5 --prompt=\"Focus on security aspects\"\n   290→```\n   291→\n   292→You can also expand all pending tasks:\n   293→\n   294→```\n   295→Please break down all pending tasks into subtasks.\n   296→```\n   297→\n   298→The agent will execute:\n   299→\n   300→```bash\n   301→task-master expand --all\n   302→```\n   303→\n   304→For research-backed subtask generation using Perplexity AI:\n   305→\n   306→```\n   307→Please break down task 5 using research-backed generation.\n   308→```\n   309→\n   310→The agent will execute:\n   311→\n   312→```bash\n   313→task-master expand --id=5 --research\n   314→```\n   315→\n   316→## Command Reference\n   317→\n   318→Here's a comprehensive reference of all available commands:\n   319→\n   320→### Parse PRD\n   321→\n   322→```bash\n   323→# Parse a PRD file and generate tasks\n   324→task-master parse-prd <prd-file.txt>\n   325→\n   326→# Limit the number of tasks generated (default is 10)\n   327→task-master parse-prd <prd-file.txt> --num-tasks=5\n   328→\n   329→# Allow task master to determine the number of tasks based on complexity\n   330→task-master parse-prd <prd-file.txt> --num-tasks=0\n   331→```\n   332→\n   333→### List Tasks\n   334→\n   335→```bash\n   336→# List all tasks\n   337→task-master list\n   338→\n   339→# List tasks with a specific status\n   340→task-master list --status=<status>\n   341→\n   342→# List tasks with subtasks\n   343→task-master list --with-subtasks\n   344→\n   345→# List tasks with a specific status and include subtasks\n   346→task-master list --status=<status> --with-subtasks\n   347→```\n   348→\n   349→### Show Next Task\n   350→\n   351→```bash\n   352→# Show the next task to work on based on dependencies and status\n   353→task-master next\n   354→```\n   355→\n   356→### Show Specific Task\n   357→\n   358→```bash\n   359→# Show details of a specific task\n   360→task-master show <id>\n   361→# or\n   362→task-master show --id=<id>\n   363→\n   364→# View a specific subtask (e.g., subtask 2 of task 1)\n   365→task-master show 1.2\n   366→```\n   367→\n   368→### Update Tasks\n   369→\n   370→```bash\n   371→# Update tasks from a specific ID and provide context\n   372→task-master update --from=<id> --prompt=\"<prompt>\"\n   373→```\n   374→\n   375→### Generate Task Files\n   376→\n   377→```bash\n   378→# Generate individual task files from tasks.json\n   379→task-master generate\n   380→```\n   381→\n   382→### Set Task Status\n   383→\n   384→```bash\n   385→# Set status of a single task\n   386→task-master set-status --id=<id> --status=<status>\n   387→\n   388→# Set status for multiple tasks\n   389→task-master set-status --id=1,2,3 --status=<status>\n   390→\n   391→# Set status for subtasks\n   392→task-master set-status --id=1.1,1.2 --status=<status>\n   393→```\n   394→\n   395→When marking a task as \"done\", all of its subtasks will automatically be marked as \"done\" as well.\n   396→\n   397→### Expand Tasks\n   398→\n   399→```bash\n   400→# Expand a specific task with subtasks\n   401→task-master expand --id=<id> --num=<number>\n   402→\n   403→# Expand a task with a dynamic number of subtasks (ignoring complexity report)\n   404→task-master expand --id=<id> --num=0\n   405→\n   406→# Expand with additional context\n   407→task-master expand --id=<id> --prompt=\"<context>\"\n   408→\n   409→# Expand all pending tasks\n   410→task-master expand --all\n   411→\n   412→# Force regeneration of subtasks for tasks that already have them\n   413→task-master expand --all --force\n   414→\n   415→# Research-backed subtask generation for a specific task\n   416→task-master expand --id=<id> --research\n   417→\n   418→# Research-backed generation for all tasks\n   419→task-master expand --all --research\n   420→```\n   421→\n   422→### Clear Subtasks\n   423→\n   424→```bash\n   425→# Clear subtasks from a specific task\n   426→task-master clear-subtasks --id=<id>\n   427→\n   428→# Clear subtasks from multiple tasks\n   429→task-master clear-subtasks --id=1,2,3\n   430→\n   431→# Clear subtasks from all tasks\n   432→task-master clear-subtasks --all\n   433→```\n   434→\n   435→### Analyze Task Complexity\n   436→\n   437→```bash\n   438→# Analyze complexity of all tasks\n   439→task-master analyze-complexity\n   440→\n   441→# Save report to a custom location\n   442→task-master analyze-complexity --output=my-report.json\n   443→\n   444→# Use a specific LLM model\n   445→task-master analyze-complexity --model=claude-3-opus-20240229\n   446→\n   447→# Set a custom complexity threshold (1-10)\n   448→task-master analyze-complexity --threshold=6\n   449→\n   450→# Use an alternative tasks file\n   451→task-master analyze-complexity --file=custom-tasks.json\n   452→\n   453→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed complexity analysis\n   454→task-master analyze-complexity --research\n   455→```\n   456→\n   457→### View Complexity Report\n   458→\n   459→```bash\n   460→# Display the task complexity analysis report\n   461→task-master complexity-report\n   462→\n   463→# View a report at a custom location\n   464→task-master complexity-report --file=my-report.json\n   465→```\n   466→\n   467→### Managing Task Dependencies\n   468→\n   469→```bash\n   470→# Add a dependency to a task\n   471→task-master add-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   472→\n   473→# Remove a dependency from a task\n   474→task-master remove-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   475→\n   476→# Validate dependencies without fixing them\n   477→task-master validate-dependencies\n   478→\n   479→# Find and fix invalid dependencies automatically\n   480→task-master fix-dependencies\n   481→```\n   482→\n   483→### Add a New Task\n   484→\n   485→```bash\n   486→# Add a new task using AI\n   487→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description of the new task\"\n   488→\n   489→# Add a task with dependencies\n   490→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description\" --dependencies=1,2,3\n   491→\n   492→# Add a task with priority\n   493→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description\" --priority=high\n   494→```\n   495→\n   496→## Feature Details\n   497→\n   498→### Analyzing Task Complexity\n   499→\n   500→The `analyze-complexity` command:\n   501→\n   502→- Analyzes each task using AI to assess its complexity on a scale of 1-10\n   503→- Recommends optimal number of subtasks based on configured DEFAULT_SUBTASKS\n   504→- Generates tailored prompts for expanding each task\n   505→- Creates a comprehensive JSON report with ready-to-use commands\n   506→- Saves the report to scripts/task-complexity-report.json by default\n   507→\n   508→The generated report contains:\n   509→\n   510→- Complexity analysis for each task (scored 1-10)\n   511→- Recommended number of subtasks based on complexity\n   512→- AI-generated expansion prompts customized for each task\n   513→- Ready-to-run expansion commands directly within each task analysis\n   514→\n   515→### Viewing Complexity Report\n   516→\n   517→The `complexity-report` command:\n   518→\n   519→- Displays a formatted, easy-to-read version of the complexity analysis report\n   520→- Shows tasks organized by complexity score (highest to lowest)\n   521→- Provides complexity distribution statistics (low, medium, high)\n   522→- Highlights tasks recommended for expansion based on threshold score\n   523→- Includes ready-to-use expansion commands for each complex task\n   524→- If no report exists, offers to generate one on the spot\n   525→\n   526→### Smart Task Expansion\n   527→\n   528→The `expand` command automatically checks for and uses the complexity report:\n   529→\n   530→When a complexity report exists:\n   531→\n   532→- Tasks are automatically expanded using the recommended subtask count and prompts\n   533→- When expanding all tasks, they're processed in order of complexity (highest first)\n   534→- Research-backed generation is preserved from the complexity analysis\n   535→- You can still override recommendations with explicit command-line options\n   536→\n   537→Example workflow:\n   538→\n   539→```bash\n   540→# Generate the complexity analysis report with research capabilities\n   541→task-master analyze-complexity --research\n   542→\n   543→# Review the report in a readable format\n   544→task-master complexity-report\n   545→\n   546→# Expand tasks using the optimized recommendations\n   547→task-master expand --id=8\n   548→# or expand all tasks\n   549→task-master expand --all\n   550→```\n   551→\n   552→### Finding the Next Task\n   553→\n   554→The `next` command:\n   555→\n   556→- Identifies tasks that are pending/in-progress and have all dependencies satisfied\n   557→- Prioritizes tasks by priority level, dependency count, and task ID\n   558→- Displays comprehensive information about the selected task:\n   559→  - Basic task details (ID, title, priority, dependencies)\n   560→  - Implementation details\n   561→  - Subtasks (if they exist)\n   562→- Provides contextual suggested actions:\n   563→  - Command to mark the task as in-progress\n   564→  - Command to mark the task as done\n   565→  - Commands for working with subtasks\n   566→\n   567→### Viewing Specific Task Details\n   568→\n   569→The `show` command:\n   570→\n   571→- Displays comprehensive details about a specific task or subtask\n   572→- Shows task status, priority, dependencies, and detailed implementation notes\n   573→- For parent tasks, displays all subtasks and their status\n   574→- For subtasks, shows parent task relationship\n   575→- Provides contextual action suggestions based on the task's state\n   576→- Works with both regular tasks and subtasks (using the format taskId.subtaskId)\n   577→\n   578→## Best Practices for AI-Driven Development\n   579→\n   580→1. **Start with a detailed PRD**: The more detailed your PRD, the better the generated tasks will be.\n   581→\n   582→2. **Review generated tasks**: After parsing the PRD, review the tasks to ensure they make sense and have appropriate dependencies.\n   583→\n   584→3. **Analyze task complexity**: Use the complexity analysis feature to identify which tasks should be broken down further.\n   585→\n   586→4. **Follow the dependency chain**: Always respect task dependencies - the Cursor agent will help with this.\n   587→\n   588→5. **Update as you go**: If your implementation diverges from the plan, use the update command to keep future tasks aligned with your current approach.\n   589→\n   590→6. **Break down complex tasks**: Use the expand command to break down complex tasks into manageable subtasks.\n   591→\n   592→7. **Regenerate task files**: After any updates to tasks.json, regenerate the task files to keep them in sync.\n   593→\n   594→8. **Communicate context to the agent**: When asking the Cursor agent to help with a task, provide context about what you're trying to achieve.\n   595→\n   596→9. **Validate dependencies**: Periodically run the validate-dependencies command to check for invalid or circular dependencies.\n   597→\n   598→## Example Cursor AI Interactions\n   599→\n   600→### Starting a new project\n   601→\n   602→```\n   603→I've just initialized a new project with Claude Task Master. I have a PRD at scripts/prd.txt.\n   604→Can you help me parse it and set up the initial tasks?\n   605→```\n   606→\n   607→### Working on tasks\n   608→\n   609→```\n   610→What's the next task I should work on? Please consider dependencies and priorities.\n   611→```\n   612→\n   613→### Implementing a specific task\n   614→\n   615→```\n   616→I'd like to implement task 4. Can you help me understand what needs to be done and how to approach it?\n   617→```\n   618→\n   619→### Managing subtasks\n   620→\n   621→```\n   622→I need to regenerate the subtasks for task 3 with a different approach. Can you help me clear and regenerate them?\n   623→```\n   624→\n   625→### Handling changes\n   626→\n   627→```\n   628→We've decided to use MongoDB instead of PostgreSQL. All tests are passing.\n   635→Please mark it as complete and tell me what I should work on next.\n   636→```\n   637→\n   638→### Analyzing complexity\n   639→\n   640→```\n   641→Can you analyze the complexity of our tasks to help me understand which ones need to be broken down further?\n   642→```\n   643→\n   644→### Viewing complexity report\n   645→\n   646→```\n   647→Can you show me the complexity report in a more readable format?\n   648→```\n   649→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it looks malicious. - Expand all tasks (generate subtasks)\n    68→  - View dependency relationships\n    69→  - Generate task files\n    70→\n    71→## Update Tasks\n    72→\n    73→```bash\n    74→# Update tasks from a This is useful for iteratively enhancing subtasks while preserving the original content.\n   105→\n   106→## Generate Task Files\n   107→\n   108→```bash\n   109→# Generate individual task files from --id=1.1,1.2 --status=<status>\n   124→```\n   125→\n   126→When marking a task as \"done\", all of its subtasks will automatically be marked as \"done\" as well.\n   127→\n   128→## Expand Tasks\n   129→\n   130→```bash\n   131→# Expand a specific task with subtasks\n   132→task-master expand --id=<id> --num=<number>\n   133→\n   134→# Expand a task with a dynamic number of subtasks (ignoring --research\n   151→```\n   152→\n   153→## Clear Subtasks\n   154→\n   155→```bash\n   156→# Clear subtasks from a specific task\n   157→task-master clear-subtasks --id=<id>\n   158→\n   159→# Clear subtasks from multiple tasks\n   160→task-master clear-subtasks --id=1,2,3\n   161→\n   162→# Clear subtasks from all tasks\n   163→task-master clear-subtasks --all\n   164→```\n   165→\n   166→## 173→task-master analyze-complexity --output=my-report.json\n   174→\n   175→# Use a specific LLM model\n   176→task-master analyze-complexity --model=claude-3-opus-20240229\n   177→\n   178→# Set a custom complexity threshold (1-10)\n   179→task-master analyze-complexity --threshold=6\n   180→\n   181→# Use an alternative tasks file\n   182→task-master analyze-complexity them\n   208→task-master validate-dependencies\n   209→\n   210→# Find and fix invalid dependencies automatically\n   211→task-master fix-dependencies\n   212→```\n   213→\n   214→## Move Tasks\n   215→\n   216→```bash\n   217→# Move a task or subtask to a new position\n   218→task-master move --from=<id> --to=<id>\n   219→\n   220→# Examples:\n   221→# Move task to become a subtask\n   222→task-master move --from=5 --to=7\n   223→\n   224→# Move subtask to become a standalone task\n   225→task-master move --from=5.2 --to=7\n   226→\n   227→# Move subtask to a different parent\n   228→task-master move --from=5.2 --to=7.3\n   229→\n   230→# Reorder subtasks within the same parent\n   231→task-master move --from=5.2 --to=5.4\n   232→\n   233→# Move a task to a new ID position (creates placeholder if doesn't exist)\n   234→task-master move --from=5 --to=25\n   235→\n   236→# Move multiple tasks at once (must have the same number of IDs)\n   237→task-master move of the new task\"\n   245→\n   246→# Add a new task using AI (research role)\n   247→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description of the new task\" --research\n   248→\n   249→# Add a task with dependencies\n   250→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description\" --dependencies=1,2,3\n   251→\n   252→# Add a task with priority\n   253→task-master add-task --prompt=\"Description\" --priority=high\n   254→```\n   255→\n   256→## Tag Management\n   257→\n   258→Task Master supports tagged task lists for multi-context task management. Each tag represents a separate, isolated context for tasks.\n   259→\n   260→```bash\n   261→# List all available tags with task counts and status\n   262→task-master tags\n   263→\n   264→# List tags with detailed metadata\n   265→task-master tags --show-metadata\n   266→\n   267→# Create a new empty tag\n   268→task-master add-tag <tag-name>\n   269→\n   270→# Create a new tag with a description\n   271→task-master add-tag <tag-name> --description=\"Feature development tasks\"\n   272→\n   273→# Create a tag based on current git branch name\n   274→task-master add-tag --from-branch\n   275→\n   276→# Create a new tag by copying tasks from the current tag\n   277→task-master add-tag <new-tag> --copy-from-current\n   278→\n   279→# Create a new tag by copying from a specific tag\n   280→task-master add-tag <new-tag> --copy-from=<source-tag>\n   281→\n   282→# Switch to a different tag context\n   283→task-master use-tag <tag-name>\n   284→\n   285→# Rename an existing tag\n   286→task-master rename-tag <old-name> <new-name>\n   287→\n   288→# Copy an entire tag to create a new one\n   289→task-master copy-tag <source-tag> <target-tag>\n   290→\n   291→# Copy a tag with a description\n   292→task-master copy-tag <source-tag> <target-tag> --description=\"Copied for testing\"\n   293→\n   294→# Delete a tag and all its tasks (with confirmation)\n   295→task-master delete-tag <tag-name>\n   296→\n   297→# Delete a tag without confirmation prompt\n   298→task-master delete-tag <tag-name> --yes\n   299→```\n   300→\n   301→**Tag Context:**\n   302→- All task operations (list, show, add, update, etc.) work within the currently active tag\n   303→- Use `--tag=<name>` flag with most commands to operate on a specific tag context\n   304→- Tags provide complete isolation - tasks in different tags don't interfere with each other\n   305→\n   306→## Initialize a Project\n   307→\n   308→```bash\n   309→# Initialize a new project with Task Master structure\n   310→task-master init\n   311→\n   312→# Initialize a new project applying specific rules\n   313→task-master init --rules cursor,windsurf,vscode\n   314→```\n   315→\n   316→- The `--rules` flag allows you to specify one or more rule profiles (e.g., `cursor`, `roo`, `windsurf`, `cline`) to apply during initialization.\n   317→- If omitted, all available rule profiles are installed by default (claude, cline, codex, cursor, roo, trae, vscode, windsurf).\n   318→- You can use multiple comma-separated profiles in a single command.\n   319→\n   320→## Manage Rules\n   321→\n   322→```bash\n   323→# Add rule profiles to your project\n   324→# (e.g., .roo/rules, .windsurf/rules)\n   325→task-master rules add <profile1,profile2,...>\n   326→\n   327→# Remove rule sets from your project\n   328→task-master rules remove <profile1,profile2,...>\n   329→\n   330→# Remove rule sets bypassing safety check (dangerous)\n   331→task-master rules remove <profile1,profile2,...> --force\n   332→\n   333→# Launch interactive rules setup to select rules\n   334→# (does not re-initialize project or ask about shell aliases)\n   335→task-master rules setup\n   336→```\n   337→\n   338→- Adding rules creates the profile and rules directory (e.g., `.roo/rules`) and copies/initializes the rules.\n   339→- Removing rules deletes the profile and rules directory and associated MCP config.\n   340→- **Safety Check**: Attempting to remove rule profiles will trigger a critical warning requiring confirmation. Use `--force` to bypass.\n   341→- You can use multiple comma-separated rules in a single command.\n   342→- The `setup` action launches an interactive prompt to select which rules to apply. The list of rules is always current with the available profiles, and no manual updates are needed. This command does **not** re-initialize your project or affect shell aliases; it only manages rules interactively.\n   343→\n   344→**Examples:**\n   345→\n   346→```bash\n   347→task-master rules add windsurf,roo,vscode\n   348→task-master rules remove windsurf\n   349→task-master rules setup\n   350→```\n   351→\n   352→### Interactive Rules Setup\n   353→\n   354→You can launch the interactive rules setup at any time with:\n   355→\n   356→```bash\n   357→task-master rules setup\n   358→```\n   359→\n   360→This command opens a prompt where you can select which rule profiles (e.g., Cursor, Roo, Windsurf) you want to add to your project. This does **not** re-initialize your project or ask about shell aliases; it only manages rules.\n   361→\n   362→- Use this command to add rule profiles interactively after project creation.\n   363→- The same interactive prompt is also used during `init` if you don't specify rules with `--rules`.\n   364→\n   365→## Configure AI Models\n   366→\n   367→```bash\n   368→# View current AI model configuration and API key status\n   369→task-master models\n   370→\n   371→# Set the primary model for generation/updates (provider inferred if known)\n   372→task-master models --set-main=claude-3-opus-20240229\n   373→\n   374→# Set the research model\n   375→task-master models --set-research=sonar-pro\n   376→\n   377→# Set the fallback model\n   378→task-master models --set-fallback=claude-3-haiku-20240307\n   379→\n   380→# Set a custom Ollama model for the main role\n   381→task-master models --set-main=my-local-llama --ollama\n   382→\n   383→# Set a custom OpenRouter model for the research role\n   384→task-master models --set-research=google/gemini-pro --openrouter\n   385→\n   386→# Run interactive setup to configure models, including custom ones\n   387→task-master models --setup\n   388→```\n   389→\n   390→Configuration is stored in `.taskmaster/config.json` in your project root (legacy `.taskmasterconfig` files are automatically migrated). API keys are still managed via `.env` or MCP configuration. Use `task-master models` without flags to see available built-in models. Use `--setup` for a guided experience.\n   391→\n   392→State is stored in `.taskmaster/state.json` in your project root. It maintains important information like the current tag. Do not manually edit this file.\n   393→\n   394→## Research Fresh Information\n   395→\n   396→```bash\n   397→# Perform AI-powered research with fresh, up-to-date information\n   398→task-master research \"What are the latest best practices for JWT authentication in Node.js?\"\n   399→\n   400→# Research with specific task context\n   401→task-master research \"How to implement OAuth 2.0?\" --id=15,16\n   402→\n   403→# Research with file context for code-aware suggestions\n   404→task-master research \"How can I optimize this API implementation?\" --files=src/api.js,src/auth.js\n   405→\n   406→# Research with custom context and project tree\n   407→task-master research \"Best practices for error handling\" --context=\"We're using Express.js\" --tree\n   408→\n   409→# Research with different detail levels\n   410→task-master research \"React Query v5 migration guide\" --detail=high\n   411→\n   412→# Disable interactive follow-up questions (useful for scripting, is the default for MCP)\n   413→# Use a custom tasks file location\n   414→task-master research \"How to implement this feature?\" --file=custom-tasks.json\n   415→\n   416→# Research within a specific tag 423→task-master research \"How to implement OAuth?\" --save-to=15\n   424→task-master research \"API optimization strategies\" --save-to=15.2\n   425→\n   426→# Combine context gathering with automatic saving of findings\n   427→task-master research \"Best practices for this implementation\" --id=15,16 --files=src/auth.js --save-to=15.3\n   428→```\n   429→\n   430→**The research command is a powerful exploration tool that provides:**\n   431→\n   432→- **Fresh information beyond AI knowledge cutoffs**\n   433→- **Project-aware context** from your tasks and files\n   434→- **Automatic task discovery** using fuzzy search\n   435→- **Multiple detail levels** (low, medium, high)\n   436→- **Token counting and cost tracking**\n   437→- **Interactive follow-up questions** for deep exploration\n   438→- **Flexible save options** (commit findings to tasks or preserve conversations)\n   439→- **Iterative discovery** through continuous questioning and refinement\n   440→\n   441→**Use research frequently to:**\n   442→\n   443→- Get current best practices before implementing features\n   444→- Research new technologies and libraries\n   445→- Find solutions to complex problems\n   446→- Validate your implementation approaches\n   447→- Stay updated with latest security recommendations\n   448→\n   449→**Interactive Features (CLI):**\n   450→\n   451→- **Follow-up questions** that maintain conversation context and allow deep exploration\n   452→- **Save menu** during or after research with flexible options:\n   453→  - **Save to task/subtask**: Commit key findings and actionable insights (recommended)\n   454→  - **Save to file**: Preserve entire conversation for later reference if needed\n   455→  - **Continue exploring**: Ask more follow-up questions {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01PyqXu1vTUx9tQWwPcLkrtJ","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Meta-Development Script\n     2→\n     3→This folder contains a **meta-development script** (`dev.js`) and related utilities that manage tasks for an AI-driven or traditional software development workflow. The script revolves around a `tasks.json` file, which holds an up-to-date list of development tasks.\n     4→\n     5→## Overview\n     6→\n     7→In an AI-driven development process—particularly with tools like [Cursor](https://www.cursor.so/)—it's beneficial to have a **single source of truth** for tasks. This script allows you to:\n     8→\n     9→1. **Parse** a PRD or requirements document (`.txt`) to initialize a set of tasks (`tasks.json`).\n    10→2. **List** all existing tasks (IDs, statuses, titles).\n    11→3. **Update** tasks to accommodate new prompts or architecture changes (useful if you discover \"implementation drift\").\n    12→4. **Generate** individual task files (e.g., `task_001.txt`) for easy reference or to feed into an AI coding workflow.\n    13→5. **Set task status**—mark tasks as `done`, `pending`, or `deferred` based on progress.\n    14→6. **Expand** tasks with subtasks—break down complex tasks into smaller, more manageable subtasks.\n    15→7. **Research-backed subtask generation**—use Perplexity AI to generate more informed and contextually relevant subtasks.\n    16→8. **Clear subtasks**—remove subtasks from specified tasks to allow regeneration or restructuring.\n    17→9. **Show task details**—display detailed information about a specific task and its subtasks.\n    18→\n    19→## Configuration\n    20→\n    21→The script can be configured through environment variables in a `.env` file at the root of the project:\n    22→\n    23→### Required Configuration\n    24→\n    25→- `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`: Your Anthropic API key for Claude\n    26→\n    27→### Optional Configuration\n    28→\n    29→- `MODEL`: Specify which Claude model to use (default: \"claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219\")\n    30→- `MAX_TOKENS`: Maximum tokens for model responses (default: 4000)\n    31→- `TEMPERATURE`: Temperature for model responses (default: 0.7)\n    32→- `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY`: Your Perplexity API key for research-backed subtask generation\n    33→- `PERPLEXITY_MODEL`: Specify which Perplexity model to use (default: \"sonar-medium-online\")\n    34→- `DEBUG`: Enable debug logging (default: false)\n    35→- `TASKMASTER_LOG_LEVEL`: Log level - debug, info, warn, error (default: info)\n    36→- `DEFAULT_SUBTASKS`: Default number of subtasks when expanding (default: 3)\n    37→- `DEFAULT_PRIORITY`: Default priority for generated tasks (default: medium)\n    38→- `PROJECT_NAME`: Override default project name in tasks.json\n    39→- `PROJECT_VERSION`: Override default version in tasks.json\n    40→\n    41→## How It Works\n    42→\n    43→1. **`tasks.json`**:\n    44→\n    45→   - A JSON file at the project root containing an array of tasks (each with `id`, `title`, `description`, `status`, etc.).\n    46→   - The `meta` field can store additional info like the project's name, version, or reference to the PRD.\n    47→   - Tasks can have `subtasks` for more detailed implementation steps.\n    48→   - Dependencies are displayed with status indicators (✅ for completed, ⏱️ for pending) to easily track progress.\n    49→\n    50→2. **Script Commands**\n    51→   You can run the script via:\n    52→\n    53→   ```bash\n    54→   node scripts/dev.js [command] [options]\n    55→   ```\n    56→\n    57→   Available commands:\n    58→\n    59→   - `parse-prd`: Generate tasks from a PRD document\n    60→   - `list`: Display all tasks with their status\n    61→   - `update`: Update tasks based on new information\n    62→   - `generate`: Create individual task files\n    63→   - `set-status`: Change a task's status\n    64→   - `expand`: Add subtasks to a task or all tasks\n    65→   - `clear-subtasks`: Remove subtasks from specified tasks\n    66→   - `next`: Determine the next task to work on based on dependencies\n    67→   - `show`: Display detailed information about a specific task\n    68→\n    69→   Run `node scripts/dev.js` without arguments to see detailed usage information.\n    70→\n    71→## Listing Tasks\n    72→\n    73→The `list` command allows you to view all tasks and their status:\n    74→\n    75→```bash\n    76→# List all tasks\n    77→node scripts/dev.js list\n    78→\n    79→# List tasks with a specific status\n    80→node scripts/dev.js list --status=pending\n    81→\n    82→# List tasks and include their subtasks\n    83→node scripts/dev.js list --with-subtasks\n    84→\n    85→# List tasks with a specific status and include their subtasks\n    86→node scripts/dev.js list --status=pending --with-subtasks\n    87→```\n    88→\n    89→## Updating Tasks\n    90→\n    91→The `update` command allows you to update tasks based on new information or implementation changes:\n    92→\n    93→```bash\n    94→# Update tasks starting from ID 4 with a new prompt\n    95→node scripts/dev.js update --from=4 --prompt=\"Refactor tasks from ID 4 onward to use Express instead of Fastify\"\n    96→\n    97→# Update all tasks (default from=1)\n    98→node scripts/dev.js update --prompt=\"Add authentication to all relevant tasks\"\n    99→\n   100→# With research-backed updates using Perplexity AI\n   101→node scripts/dev.js update --from=4 --prompt=\"Integrate OAuth 2.0\" --research\n   102→\n   103→# Specify a different tasks file\n   104→node scripts/dev.js update --file=custom-tasks.json --from=5 --prompt=\"Change database from MongoDB to PostgreSQL\"\n   105→```\n   106→\n   107→Notes:\n   108→\n   109→- The `--prompt` parameter is required and should explain the changes or new context\n   110→- Only tasks that aren't marked as 'done' will be updated\n   111→- Tasks with ID >= the specified --from value will be updated\n   112→- The `--research` flag uses Perplexity AI for more informed updates when available\n   113→\n   114→## Updating a Single Task\n   115→\n   116→The `update-task` command allows you to update a specific task instead of multiple tasks:\n   117→\n   118→```bash\n   119→# Update a specific task with new information\n   120→node scripts/dev.js update-task --id=4 --prompt=\"Use JWT for authentication\"\n   121→\n   122→# With research-backed updates using Perplexity AI\n   123→node scripts/dev.js update-task --id=4 --prompt=\"Use JWT for authentication\" --research\n   124→```\n   125→\n   126→This command:\n   127→\n   128→- Updates only the specified task rather than a range of tasks\n   129→- Provides detailed validation with helpful error messages\n   130→- Checks for required API keys when using research mode\n   131→- Falls back gracefully if Perplexity API is unavailable\n   132→- Preserves tasks that are already marked as \"done\"\n   133→- Includes contextual error handling for common issues\n   134→\n   135→## Setting Task Status\n   136→\n   137→The `set-status` command allows you to change a task's status:\n   138→\n   139→```bash\n   140→# Mark a task as done\n   141→node scripts/dev.js set-status --id=3 --status=done\n   142→\n   143→# Mark a task as pending\n   144→node scripts/dev.js set-status --id=4 --status=pending\n   145→\n   146→# Mark a specific subtask as done\n   147→node scripts/dev.js set-status --id=3.1 --status=done\n   148→\n   149→# Mark multiple tasks at once\n   150→node scripts/dev.js set-status --id=1,2,3 --status=done\n   151→```\n   152→\n   153→Notes:\n   154→\n   155→- When marking a parent task as \"done\", all of its subtasks will automatically be marked as \"done\" as well\n   156→- Common status values are 'done', 'pending', and 'deferred', but any string is accepted\n   157→- You can specify multiple task IDs by separating them with commas\n   158→- Subtask IDs are specified using the format `parentId.subtaskId` (e.g., `3.1`)\n   159→- Dependencies are updated to show completion status (✅ for completed, ⏱️ for pending) throughout the system\n   160→\n   161→## Expanding Tasks\n   162→\n   163→The `expand` command allows you to break down tasks into subtasks for more detailed implementation:\n   164→\n   165→```bash\n   166→# Expand a specific task with 3 subtasks (default)\n   167→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=3\n   168→\n   169→# Expand a specific task with 5 subtasks\n   170→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=3 --num=5\n   171→\n   172→# Expand a task with additional context\n   173→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=3 --prompt=\"Focus on security aspects\"\n   174→\n   175→# Expand all pending tasks that don't have subtasks\n   176→node scripts/dev.js expand --all\n   177→\n   178→# Force regeneration of subtasks for all pending tasks\n   179→node scripts/dev.js expand --all --force\n   180→\n   181→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed subtask generation\n   182→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=3 --research\n   183→\n   184→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed generation on all pending tasks\n   185→node scripts/dev.js expand --all --research\n   186→```\n   187→\n   188→## Clearing Subtasks\n   189→\n   190→The `clear-subtasks` command allows you to remove subtasks from specified tasks:\n   191→\n   192→```bash\n   193→# Clear subtasks from a specific task\n   194→node scripts/dev.js clear-subtasks --id=3\n   195→\n   196→# Clear subtasks from multiple tasks\n   197→node scripts/dev.js clear-subtasks --id=1,2,3\n   198→\n   199→# Clear subtasks from all tasks\n   200→node scripts/dev.js clear-subtasks --all\n   201→```\n   202→\n   203→Notes:\n   204→\n   205→- After clearing subtasks, task files are automatically regenerated\n   206→- This is useful when you want to regenerate subtasks with a different approach\n   207→- Can be combined with the `expand` command to immediately generate new subtasks\n   208→- Works with both parent tasks and individual subtasks\n   209→\n   210→## AI Integration\n   211→\n   212→The script integrates with two AI services:\n   213→\n   214→1. **Anthropic Claude**: Used for parsing PRDs, generating tasks, and creating subtasks.\n   215→2. **Perplexity AI**: Used for research-backed subtask generation when the `--research` flag is specified.\n   216→\n   217→The Perplexity integration uses the OpenAI client to connect to Perplexity's API, which provides enhanced research capabilities for generating more informed subtasks. If the Perplexity API is unavailable or encounters an error, the script will automatically fall back to using Anthropic's Claude.\n   218→\n   219→To use the Perplexity integration:\n   220→\n   221→1. Obtain a Perplexity API key\n   222→2. Add `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY` to your `.env` file\n   223→3. Optionally specify `PERPLEXITY_MODEL` in your `.env` file (default: \"sonar-medium-online\")\n   224→4. Use the `--research` flag with the `expand` command\n   225→\n   226→## Logging\n   227→\n   228→The script supports different logging levels controlled by the `TASKMASTER_LOG_LEVEL` environment variable:\n   229→\n   230→- `debug`: Detailed information, typically useful for troubleshooting\n   231→- `info`: Confirmation that things are working as expected (default)\n   232→- `warn`: Warning messages that don't prevent execution\n   233→- `error`: Error messages that might prevent execution\n   234→\n   235→When `DEBUG=true` is set, debug logs are also written to a `dev-debug.log` file in the project root.\n   236→\n   237→## Managing Task Dependencies\n   238→\n   239→The `add-dependency` and `remove-dependency` commands allow you to manage task dependencies:\n   240→\n   241→```bash\n   242→# Add a dependency to a task\n   243→node scripts/dev.js add-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   244→\n   245→# Remove a dependency from a task\n   246→node scripts/dev.js remove-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   247→```\n   248→\n   249→These commands:\n   250→\n   251→1. **Allow precise dependency management**:\n   252→\n   253→   - Add dependencies between tasks with automatic validation\n   254→   - Remove dependencies when they're no longer needed\n   255→   - Update task files automatically after changes\n   256→\n   257→2. **Include validation checks**:\n   258→\n   259→   - Prevent circular dependencies (a task depending on itself)\n   260→   - Prevent duplicate dependencies\n   261→   - Verify that both tasks exist before adding/removing dependencies\n   262→   - Check if dependencies exist before attempting to remove them\n   263→\n   264→3. **Provide clear feedback**:\n   265→\n   266→   - Success messages confirm when dependencies are added/removed\n   267→   - Error messages explain why operations failed (if applicable)\n   268→\n   269→4. **Automatically update task files**:\n   270→   - Regenerates task files to reflect dependency changes\n   271→   - Ensures tasks and their files stay synchronized\n   272→\n   273→## Dependency Validation and Fixing\n   274→\n   275→The script provides two specialized commands to ensure task dependencies remain valid and properly maintained:\n   276→\n   277→### Validating Dependencies\n   278→\n   279→The `validate-dependencies` command allows you to check for invalid dependencies without making changes:\n   280→\n   281→```bash\n   282→# Check for invalid dependencies in tasks.json\n   283→node scripts/dev.js validate-dependencies\n   284→\n   285→# Specify a different tasks file\n   286→node scripts/dev.js validate-dependencies --file=custom-tasks.json\n   287→```\n   288→\n   289→This command:\n   290→\n   291→- Scans all tasks and subtasks for non-existent dependencies\n   292→- Identifies potential self-dependencies (tasks referencing themselves)\n   293→- Reports all found issues without modifying files\n   294→- Provides a comprehensive summary of dependency state\n   295→- Gives detailed statistics on task dependencies\n   296→\n   297→Use this command to audit your task structure before applying fixes.\n   298→\n   299→### Fixing Dependencies\n   300→\n   301→The `fix-dependencies` command proactively finds and fixes all invalid dependencies:\n   302→\n   303→```bash\n   304→# Find and fix all invalid dependencies\n   305→node scripts/dev.js fix-dependencies\n   306→\n   307→# Specify a different tasks file\n   308→node scripts/dev.js fix-dependencies --file=custom-tasks.json\n   309→```\n   310→\n   311→This command:\n   312→\n   313→1. **Validates all dependencies** across tasks and subtasks\n   314→2. **Automatically removes**:\n   315→   - References to non-existent tasks and subtasks\n   316→   - Self-dependencies (tasks depending on themselves)\n   317→3. **Fixes issues in both**:\n   318→   - The tasks.json data structure\n   319→   - Individual task files during regeneration\n   320→4. **Provides a detailed report**:\n   321→   - Types of issues fixed (non-existent vs. self-dependencies)\n   322→   - Number of tasks affected (tasks vs. subtasks)\n   323→   - Where fixes were applied (tasks.json vs. task files)\n   324→   - List of all individual fixes made\n   325→\n   326→This is especially useful when tasks have been deleted or IDs have changed, potentially breaking dependency chains.\n   327→\n   328→## Analyzing Task Complexity\n   329→\n   330→The `analyze-complexity` command allows you to automatically assess task complexity and generate expansion recommendations:\n   331→\n   332→```bash\n   333→# Analyze all tasks and generate expansion recommendations\n   334→node scripts/dev.js analyze-complexity\n   335→\n   336→# Specify a custom output file\n   337→node scripts/dev.js analyze-complexity --output=custom-report.json\n   338→\n   339→# Override the model used for analysis\n   340→node scripts/dev.js analyze-complexity --model=claude-3-opus-20240229\n   341→\n   342→# Set a custom complexity threshold (1-10)\n   343→node scripts/dev.js analyze-complexity --threshold=6\n   344→\n   345→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed complexity analysis\n   346→node scripts/dev.js analyze-complexity --research\n   347→```\n   348→\n   349→Notes:\n   350→\n   351→- The command uses Claude to analyze each task's complexity (or Perplexity with --research flag)\n   352→- Tasks are scored on a scale of 1-10\n   353→- Each task receives a recommended number of subtasks based on DEFAULT_SUBTASKS configuration\n   354→- The default output path is `scripts/task-complexity-report.json`\n   355→- Each task in the analysis includes a ready-to-use `expansionCommand` that can be copied directly to the terminal or executed programmatically\n   356→- Tasks with complexity scores below the threshold (default: 5) may not need expansion\n   357→- The research flag provides more contextual and informed complexity assessments\n   358→\n   359→### Integration with Expand Command\n   360→\n   361→The `expand` command automatically checks for and uses complexity analysis if available:\n   362→\n   363→```bash\n   364→# Expand a task, using complexity report recommendations if available\n   365→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=8\n   366→\n   367→# Expand all tasks, prioritizing by complexity score if a report exists\n   368→node scripts/dev.js expand --all\n   369→\n   370→# Override recommendations with explicit values\n   371→node scripts/dev.js expand --id=8 --num=5 --prompt=\"Custom prompt\"\n   372→```\n   373→\n   374→When a complexity report exists:\n   375→\n   376→- The `expand` command will use the recommended subtask count from the report (unless overridden)\n   377→- It will use the tailored expansion prompt from the report (unless a custom prompt is provided)\n   378→- When using `--all`, tasks are sorted by complexity score (highest first)\n   379→- The `--research` flag is preserved from the complexity analysis to expansion\n   380→\n   381→The output report structure is:\n   382→\n   383→```json\n   384→{\n   385→ \"meta\": {\n   386→  \"generatedAt\": \"2023-06-15T12:34:56.789Z\",\n   387→  \"tasksAnalyzed\": 20,\n   388→  \"thresholdScore\": 5,\n   389→  \"projectName\": \"Your Project Name\",\n   390→  \"usedResearch\": true\n   391→ },\n   392→ \"complexityAnalysis\": [\n   393→  {\n   394→   \"taskId\": 8,\n   395→   \"taskTitle\": \"Develop Implementation Drift Handling\",\n   396→   \"complexityScore\": 9.5,\n   397→   \"recommendedSubtasks\": 6,\n   398→   \"expansionPrompt\": \"Create subtasks that handle detecting...\",\n   399→   \"reasoning\": \"This task requires sophisticated logic...\",\n   400→   \"expansionCommand\": \"node scripts/dev.js expand --id=8 --num=6 --prompt=\\\"Create subtasks...\\\" --research\"\n   401→  }\n   402→  // More tasks sorted by complexity score (highest first)\n   403→ ]\n   404→}\n   405→```\n   406→\n   407→## Finding the Next Task\n   408→\n   409→The `next` command helps you determine which task to work on next based on dependencies and status:\n   410→\n   411→```bash\n   412→# Show the next task to work on\n   413→node scripts/dev.js next\n   414→\n   415→# Specify a different tasks file\n   416→node scripts/dev.js next --file=custom-tasks.json\n   417→```\n   418→\n   419→This command:\n   420→\n   421→1. Identifies all **eligible tasks** - pending or in-progress tasks whose dependencies are all satisfied (marked as done)\n   422→2. **Prioritizes** these eligible tasks by:\n   423→   - Priority level (high > medium > low)\n   424→   - Number of dependencies (fewer dependencies first)\n   425→   - Task ID (lower ID first)\n   426→3. **Displays** comprehensive information about the selected task:\n   427→   - Basic task details (ID, title, priority, dependencies)\n   428→   - Detailed description and implementation details\n   429→   - Subtasks if they exist\n   430→4. Provides **contextual suggested actions**:\n   431→   - Command to mark the task as in-progress\n   432→   - Command to mark the task as done when completed\n   433→   - Commands for working with subtasks (update status or expand)\n   434→\n   435→This feature ensures you're always working on the most appropriate task based on your project's current state and dependency structure.\n   436→\n   437→## Showing Task Details\n   438→\n   439→The `show` command allows you to view detailed information about a specific task:\n   440→\n   441→```bash\n   442→# Show details for a specific task\n   443→node scripts/dev.js show 1\n   444→\n   445→# Alternative syntax with --id option\n   446→node scripts/dev.js show --id=1\n   447→\n   448→# Show details for a subtask\n   449→node scripts/dev.js show --id=1.2\n   450→\n   451→# Specify a different tasks file\n   452→node scripts/dev.js show 3 --file=custom-tasks.json\n   453→```\n   454→\n   455→This command:\n   456→\n   457→1. **Displays {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01PyNbM1DtEF3Qs7trKeBPXU","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Meta-Development Script\n     2→\n     3→This folder contains a **meta-development script** (`dev.js`) and related utilities that manage tasks for an AI-driven or traditional software development workflow. The script revolves around a `tasks.json` file, which holds an up-to-date list of development tasks.\n     4→\n     5→## Overview\n     6→\n     7→In an AI-driven development process—particularly with tools like [Cursor](https://www.cursor.so/)—it's beneficial to have a **single source of truth** for tasks. This script allows you to:\n     8→\n     9→1. **Parse** a PRD or requirements document (`.txt`) to initialize a set of tasks (`tasks.json`).\n    10→2. **List** all existing tasks (IDs, statuses, titles).\n    11→3. **Update** tasks to accommodate new prompts or architecture changes (useful if you discover \"implementation drift\").\n    12→4. **Generate** individual task files (e.g., `task_001.txt`) for easy reference or to feed into an AI coding workflow.\n    13→5. **Set task status**—mark tasks as `done`, `pending`, or `deferred` based on progress.\n    14→6. **Expand** tasks with subtasks—break down complex tasks into smaller, more manageable subtasks.\n    15→7. **Research-backed subtask generation**—use Perplexity AI to generate more informed and contextually relevant subtasks.\n    16→8. **Clear subtasks**—remove subtasks from specified tasks to allow regeneration or restructuring.\n    17→9. **Show task details**—display detailed information about a specific task and its subtasks.\n    18→\n    19→## Configuration (Updated)\n    20→\n    21→Task Master configuration is now managed through two primary methods:\n    22→\n    23→1.  **`.taskmaster/config.json` File (Project Root - Primary)**\n    24→\n    25→    - Stores AI model selections (`main`, `research`, `fallback`), model parameters (`maxTokens`, `temperature`), `logLevel`, `defaultSubtasks`, `defaultPriority`, `projectName`, etc.\n    26→    - Managed using the `task-master models --setup` command or the `models` MCP tool.\n    27→    - This is the main configuration file for most settings.\n    28→\n    29→2.  **Environment Variables (`.env` File - API Keys Only)**\n    30→    - Used **only** for sensitive **API Keys** (e.g., `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY`).\n    31→    - Create a `.env` file in your project root for CLI usage.\n    32→    - See `assets/env.example` for required key names.\n    33→\n    34→**Important:** Settings like `MODEL`, `MAX_TOKENS`, `TEMPERATURE`, `TASKMASTER_LOG_LEVEL`, etc., are **no longer set via `.env`**. Use `task-master models --setup` instead.\n    35→\n    36→## How It Works\n    37→\n    38→1. **`tasks.json`**:\n    39→\n    40→   - A JSON file at the project root containing an array of tasks (each with `id`, `title`, `description`, `status`, etc.).\n    41→   - The `meta` field can store additional info like the project's name, version, or reference to the PRD.\n    42→   - Tasks can have `subtasks` for more detailed implementation steps.\n    43→   - Dependencies are displayed with status indicators (✅ for completed, ⏱️ for pending) to easily track progress.\n    44→\n    45→2. **CLI Commands**\n    46→   You can run the commands via:\n    47→\n    48→   ```bash\n    49→   # If installed globally\n    50→   task-master [command] [options]\n    51→\n    52→   # If using locally within the project\n    53→   node scripts/dev.js [command] [options]\n    54→   ```\n    55→\n    56→   Available commands:\n    57→\n    58→   - `init`: Initialize a new project\n    59→   - `parse-prd`: Generate tasks from a PRD document\n    60→   - `list`: Display all tasks with their status\n    61→   - `update`: Update tasks based on new information\n    62→   - `generate`: Create individual task files\n    63→   - `set-status`: Change a task's status\n    64→   - `expand`: Add subtasks to a task or all tasks\n    65→   - `clear-subtasks`: Remove subtasks from specified tasks\n    66→   - `next`: Determine the next task to work on based on dependencies\n    67→   - `show`: Display detailed information about a specific task\n    68→   - `analyze-complexity`: Analyze task complexity and generate recommendations\n    69→   - `complexity-report`: Display the complexity analysis in a readable format\n    70→   - `add-dependency`: Add a dependency between tasks\n    71→   - `remove-dependency`: Remove a dependency from a task\n    72→   - `validate-dependencies`: Check for invalid dependencies\n    73→   - `fix-dependencies`: Fix invalid dependencies automatically\n    74→   - `add-task`: Add a new task using AI\n    75→\n    76→   Run `task-master --help` or `node scripts/dev.js --help` to see detailed usage information.\n    77→\n    78→## Listing Tasks\n    79→\n    80→The `list` command allows you to view all tasks and their status:\n    81→\n    82→```bash\n    83→# List all tasks\n    84→task-master list\n    85→\n    86→# List tasks with a specific status\n    87→task-master list --status=pending\n    88→\n    89→# List tasks and include their subtasks\n    90→task-master list --with-subtasks\n    91→\n    92→# List tasks with a specific status and include their subtasks\n    93→task-master list --status=pending --with-subtasks\n    94→```\n    95→\n    96→## Updating Tasks\n    97→\n    98→The `update` command allows you to update tasks based on new information or implementation changes:\n    99→\n   100→```bash\n   101→# Update tasks starting from ID 4 with a new prompt\n   102→task-master update --from=4 --prompt=\"Refactor tasks from ID 4 onward to use Express instead of Fastify\"\n   103→\n   104→# Update all tasks (default from=1)\n   105→task-master update --prompt=\"Add authentication to all relevant tasks\"\n   106→\n   107→# Specify a different tasks file\n   108→task-master update --file=custom-tasks.json --from=5 --prompt=\"Change database from MongoDB to PostgreSQL\"\n   109→```\n   110→\n   111→Notes:\n   112→\n   113→- The `--prompt` parameter is required and should explain the changes or new context\n   114→- Only tasks that aren't marked as 'done' will be updated\n   115→- Tasks with ID >= the specified --from value will be updated\n   116→\n   117→## Setting Task Status\n   118→\n   119→The `set-status` command allows you to change a task's status:\n   120→\n   121→```bash\n   122→# Mark a task as done\n   123→task-master set-status --id=3 --status=done\n   124→\n   125→# Mark a task as pending\n   126→task-master set-status --id=4 --status=pending\n   127→\n   128→# Mark a specific subtask as done\n   129→task-master set-status --id=3.1 --status=done\n   130→\n   131→# Mark multiple tasks at once\n   132→task-master set-status --id=1,2,3 --status=done\n   133→```\n   134→\n   135→Notes:\n   136→\n   137→- When marking a parent task as \"done\", all of its subtasks will automatically be marked as \"done\" as well\n   138→- Common status values are 'done', 'pending', and 'deferred', but any string is accepted\n   139→- You can specify multiple task IDs by separating them with commas\n   140→- Subtask IDs are specified using the format `parentId.subtaskId` (e.g., `3.1`)\n   141→- Dependencies are updated to show completion status (✅ for completed, ⏱️ for pending) throughout the system\n   142→\n   143→## Expanding Tasks\n   144→\n   145→The `expand` command allows you to break down tasks into subtasks for more detailed implementation:\n   146→\n   147→```bash\n   148→# Expand a specific task with 3 subtasks (default)\n   149→task-master expand --id=3\n   150→\n   151→# aspects\"\n   156→\n   157→# Expand all pending tasks that don't have subtasks\n   158→task-master expand --all\n   159→\n   160→# Force regeneration of subtasks for all pending tasks\n   161→task-master expand --all --force\n   162→\n   163→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed subtask generation\n   164→task-master expand --id=3 --research\n   165→\n   166→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed generation on all pending tasks\n   167→task-master expand --all --research\n   168→```\n   169→\n   170→## Clearing Subtasks\n   171→\n   172→The `clear-subtasks` command allows you to remove subtasks from specified tasks:\n   173→\n   174→```bash\n   175→# Clear subtasks from a specific task\n   176→task-master clear-subtasks --id=3\n   177→\n   178→# Clear subtasks from multiple tasks\n   179→task-master clear-subtasks --id=1,2,3\n   180→\n   181→# Clear subtasks from all tasks\n   182→task-master clear-subtasks --all\n   183→```\n   184→\n   185→Notes:\n   186→\n   187→- After clearing subtasks, task files are automatically regenerated\n   188→- This is useful when you want to regenerate subtasks with a different approach\n   189→- Can be combined with the `expand` command to immediately generate new subtasks\n   190→- Works with both parent tasks and individual subtasks\n   191→\n   192→## AI Integration (Updated)\n   193→\n   194→- The script now uses a unified AI service layer (`ai-services-unified.js`).\n   195→- Model selection (e.g., Claude vs. Perplexity for `--research`) is determined by the configuration in `.taskmaster/config.json` based on the requested `role` (`main` or `research`).\n   196→- API keys are automatically resolved from your `.env` file (for CLI) or MCP session environment.\n   197→- To use the research capabilities (e.g., `expand --research`), ensure you have:\n   198→  1.  Configured a model for the `research` role using `task-master models --setup` (Perplexity models are recommended).\n   199→  2.  Added the corresponding API key (e.g., `PERPLEXITY_API_KEY`) to your `.env` file.\n   200→\n   201→## Logging\n   202→\n   203→The script supports different logging levels controlled by the `TASKMASTER_LOG_LEVEL` environment variable:\n   204→\n   205→- `debug`: Detailed information, typically useful for troubleshooting\n   206→- `info`: Confirmation that things are working as expected (default)\n   207→- `warn`: Warning messages that don't prevent execution\n   208→- `error`: Error messages that might prevent execution\n   209→\n   210→When `DEBUG=true` is set, debug logs are also written to a `dev-debug.log` file in the project root.\n   211→\n   212→## Managing Task Dependencies\n   213→\n   214→The `add-dependency` and `remove-dependency` commands allow you to manage task dependencies:\n   215→\n   216→```bash\n   217→# Add a dependency to a task\n   218→task-master add-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   219→\n   220→# Remove a dependency from a task\n   221→task-master remove-dependency --id=<id> --depends-on=<id>\n   222→```\n   223→\n   224→These commands:\n   225→\n   226→1. **Allow precise dependency management**:\n   227→\n   228→   - Add dependencies between tasks with automatic validation\n   229→   - Remove dependencies when they're no longer needed\n   230→   - Update task files automatically after changes\n   231→\n   232→2. **Include validation checks**:\n   233→\n   234→   - Prevent circular dependencies (a task depending on itself)\n   235→   - Prevent duplicate dependencies\n   236→   - Verify that both tasks exist before adding/removing dependencies\n   237→   - Check if dependencies exist before attempting to remove them\n   238→\n   239→3. **Provide clear feedback**:\n   240→\n   241→   - Success messages confirm when dependencies are added/removed\n   242→   - Error messages explain why operations failed (if applicable)\n   243→\n   244→4. **Automatically update task files**:\n   245→   - Regenerates task files to reflect dependency changes\n   246→   - Ensures tasks and their files stay synchronized\n   247→\n   248→## Dependency Validation and Fixing\n   249→\n   250→The script provides two specialized commands to ensure task dependencies remain valid and properly maintained:\n   251→\n   252→### Validating Dependencies\n   253→\n   254→The `validate-dependencies` command allows you to check for invalid dependencies without making changes:\n   255→\n   256→```bash\n   257→# Check for invalid dependencies in tasks.json\n   258→task-master validate-dependencies\n   259→\n   260→# Specify a different tasks file\n   261→task-master validate-dependencies --file=custom-tasks.json\n   262→```\n   263→\n   264→This command:\n   265→\n   266→- Scans all tasks and subtasks for non-existent dependencies\n   267→- Identifies potential self-dependencies (tasks referencing themselves)\n   268→- Reports all found issues without modifying files\n   269→- Provides a comprehensive summary of dependency state\n   270→- Gives detailed statistics on task dependencies\n   271→\n   272→Use this command to audit your task structure before applying fixes.\n   273→\n   274→### Fixing Dependencies\n   275→\n   276→The `fix-dependencies` command proactively finds and fixes all invalid dependencies:\n   277→\n   278→```bash\n   279→# Find and fix all invalid dependencies\n   280→task-master fix-dependencies\n   281→\n   282→# Specify a different tasks file\n   283→task-master fix-dependencies --file=custom-tasks.json\n   284→```\n   285→\n   286→This command:\n   287→\n   288→1. **Validates all dependencies** across tasks and subtasks\n   289→2. **Automatically removes**:\n   290→   - References to non-existent tasks and subtasks\n   291→   - Self-dependencies (tasks depending on themselves)\n   292→3. **Fixes issues in both**:\n   293→   - The tasks.json data structure\n   294→   - Individual task files during regeneration\n   295→4. **Provides a detailed report**:\n   296→   - Types of issues fixed (non-existent vs. self-dependencies)\n   297→   - Number of tasks affected (tasks vs. subtasks)\n   298→   - Where fixes were applied (tasks.json vs. task files)\n   299→   - List of all individual fixes made\n   300→\n   301→This is especially useful when tasks have been deleted or IDs have changed, potentially breaking dependency chains.\n   302→\n   303→## Analyzing Task Complexity\n   304→\n   305→The `analyze-complexity` command allows you to automatically assess task complexity and generate expansion recommendations:\n   306→\n   307→```bash\n   308→# Analyze all tasks and generate expansion recommendations\n   309→task-master analyze-complexity\n   310→\n   311→# Specify a custom output file\n   312→task-master analyze-complexity --output=custom-report.json\n   313→\n   314→# Override the model used for analysis\n   315→task-master analyze-complexity --model=claude-3-opus-20240229\n   316→\n   317→# Set a custom complexity threshold (1-10)\n   318→task-master analyze-complexity --threshold=6\n   319→\n   320→# Use Perplexity AI for research-backed complexity analysis\n   321→task-master analyze-complexity --research\n   322→```\n   323→\n   324→Notes:\n   325→\n   326→- The command uses Claude to analyze each task's complexity (or Perplexity with --research flag)\n   327→- Tasks are scored on a scale of 1-10\n   328→- Each task receives a recommended number of subtasks based on DEFAULT_SUBTASKS configuration\n   329→- The default output path is `scripts/task-complexity-report.json`\n   330→- Each task in the analysis includes a ready-to-use `expansionCommand` that can be copied directly to the terminal or executed programmatically\n   331→- Tasks with complexity scores below the threshold (default: 5) may not need expansion\n   332→- The research flag provides more contextual and informed complexity assessments\n   333→\n   334→### Integration with Expand Command\n   335→\n   336→The `expand` command automatically checks for and uses complexity analysis if available:\n   337→\n   338→```bash\n   339→# Expand a task, using complexity report recommendations if available\n   340→task-master expand --id=8\n   341→\n   342→# Expand all tasks, prioritizing by complexity score if a report exists\n   343→task-master expand --all\n   344→\n   345→# Override recommendations with explicit values\n   346→task-master expand --id=8 --num=5 --prompt=\"Custom prompt\"\n   347→```\n   348→\n   349→When a complexity report exists:\n   350→\n   351→- The `expand` command will use the recommended subtask count from the report (unless overridden)\n   352→- It will use the tailored expansion prompt from the report (unless a custom prompt is provided)\n   353→- When using `--all`, tasks are sorted by complexity score (highest first)\n   354→- The `--research` flag is preserved from the complexity analysis to expansion\n   355→\n   356→The output report structure is:\n   357→\n   358→```json\n   359→{\n   360→  \"meta\": {\n   361→    \"generatedAt\": \"2023-06-15T12:34:56.789Z\",\n   362→    \"tasksAnalyzed\": 20,\n   363→    \"thresholdScore\": 5,\n   364→    \"projectName\": \"Your Project Name\",\n   365→    \"usedResearch\": true\n   366→  },\n   367→  \"complexityAnalysis\": [\n   368→    {\n   369→      \"taskId\": 8,\n   370→      \"taskTitle\": \"Develop Implementation Drift Handling\",\n   371→      \"complexityScore\": 9.5,\n   372→      \"recommendedSubtasks\": 6,\n   373→      \"expansionPrompt\": \"Create subtasks that handle detecting...\",\n   374→      \"reasoning\": \"This task requires sophisticated logic...\",\n   375→      \"expansionCommand\": \"task-master expand --id=8 --num=6 --prompt=\\\"Create subtasks...\\\" --research\"\n   376→    }\n   377→    // More tasks sorted by complexity score (highest first)\n   378→  ]\n   379→}\n   380→```\n   381→\n   382→## Finding the Next Task\n   383→\n   384→The `next` command helps you determine Task Completion\">\n    49→    When a task is completed, tell the agent:\n    50→\n    51→    ```\n    52→    Task 3 is now complete. We're now using Express instead of Fastify.
